karakteristiek Bijlage 7 Analyse resultaten houtskoolonderzoek gebied XVI 94 95 Bijlage 8 Natuurkundig en chemisch onderzoek gebied XVI Bijlage 8a MATERIALS nano TECHNOLOGY Prof . 
Jerzy J. Langer , FRSC Mickiewicz University at Poznañ , Faculty of Chemistry Laboratory for Materials Physicochemistry and Nanotechnology Grunwaldzka 10 * PL-63100 Srem * Poland FAX : +4861 2833622 Tel . 
: +4861 2833511 orsel @ sigmaxi.net Physico-chemical studies on charred archaeological sample of Drontermeer Interim report ( 28.03.2009 ) Samples of black organic materials examined : Sr 765 - Drontermeer , hearthpit 10 ( vnr . 
7 ) , mesolith ; Sr 766 - Drontermeer , hearthpit 11 ( vnr . 
14 ) , mesolith Sr 767 - Drontermeer , hearthpit 5 ( vnr . 
32 ) , mesolith ; Sr 768 - Drontermeer , hearthpit 1 ( vnr . 
36 ) , mesolith . 
Sr 769 - Drontermeer , hearthpit 3 ( vnr . 
37 ) , mesolith . 
Sr 770 - Drontermeer , hearthpit 2 ( vnr . 
40 ) , mesolith . 
The samples are insoluble in common organic solvents , in water and aqueous solutions of NaOH ( pH 13 ) and HCl ( pH 1 ) . 
Thermal stability of the samples was examined with a microscope equipped with the heater ( PHMK 05 apparatus for melting point measurements ) . 
All the sample Sr765–Sr770 are resistant against heating up to 300 oC ( no melting or softening is observed ) . 
It means , that the material was formed at the temperature far above 300 oC and carbonised to a high degree . 
The conclusion is strongly supported by microscope observations . 
The optical microscope examination ( with BIOLAR Polarizing Interference Microscope , PZO ) of samples ( Sr 765 – 770 ) shows a structure , which is typical for charred wood , similar to that observed in today ’ s charcoal ( WD ) , with traces of charring porous glassy material . 
A cell structure was observed , together with inclusions of a tar in the form typical for wood decomposed at a high temperature without oxygen . 
The infrared spectra ( FTIR ) are measured with Bruker IFS 66v/S spectrometer . 
We observe a strong and very broad absorption band ( 3700-1800 cm-1 ) with a maximum at 3364-3330 cm-1 , which is typical for OH hydrogen bonding system , but also for highly carbonized materials of a conjugated •-electron system . 
Very weak peaks are observed in the range of 2850-2970 cm-1 associated with vibrations of CH2 and CH3 groups . 
The absorption in the range of 1000-1700 cm-1 is assigned to well defined molecular structures , e.g . 
carboxylic acid salts ( 1577 and 1380 cm-1 , COO- ) , C-O bonds ( ~1250 , ~1175 , ~1085 and 1040 cm-1 ) , aromatic rings ( 1550-1600 cm-1 , 975 , 840-850 , 800 and 780 cm-1 ) . 
Such well defined absorption peaks are not observed in today ’ s charcoal ( WD ) due to thermal destruction of most molecules and functional groups at the temperature of 900oC . 
We found a low concentration of carboxylic acids ( COOH groups ) , mostly unsaturated aromatic structures of a typical absorption at 1700-1710 cm-1 . 
Organic salts are the main components detected in all samples due to a characteristic IR absorption owing to asymmetric vibrations of carboxylic groups ( -COO- ) at 1570-1575 cm-1 for aromatic and nonaromatic unsaturated salts . 
Absorption assigned to symmetric vibrations of COO- is observed at 13631384 cm-1 . 
Taking into account a degree of unsaturation , which is associated with the vibration energy ( the higher unsaturation , the lower vibration energy and the wave number of the corresponding absorption band ) , the sample examined can be assigned to partly unsaturated materials . 
This is a function of chemical composition of a starting material and the temperature of carbonization . 
An absorption at 1040-1250 cm-1 is assigned to vibrations of C-O bonds . 
In all samples a relatively low level of inorganic impurities ( e.g Si-O bonds ) is detected . 
There is no correlation of FTIR data with the reference typical birch wood tar ( BWT ) , except for Sr765 ( Vnr . 
7 ) , where a very weak absorption at 880 and 730 cm-1 can be assigned to BWT , however no other evidence is available for such a possibility ( hypothesis ) . 
96 The results of XRF analysis show that Ca-containing compounds are the main inorganic contaminants in the samples Sr 765 ( vnr . 
7 ) and Sr 770 ( vnr . 
40 ) . 
The ratio of Fe/Ca amounts to 0.23 , and 0.81 for Sr 765 ( vnr . 
7 ) and Sr 770 ( vnr . 
40 ) , respectively . 
To conclude , the samples examined Sr 765 - Sr 770 are charred organic materials : wood and wood tar pitch charred at a very high temperature ( far above 300oC ) , but lower than that typical for today ’ s charcoal ( e.g . 
900oC ) . 
All the samples were formed in a process with a limited access to the air ( oxygen ) and in that sense were intentionally fabricated . 
Properties of all the samples Sr765-770 are related to charcoal , but also in a part to highly carbonised heavy fractions of wood tar ( pitch ) , both most likely fabricated in intentionally performed processes with a controlled access to oxygen ( air ) . 
The charcoal and pitch , produced at the same time , were probably prepared from the pinewood , but it is not conclusively evidenced . 
Generally , we didn ’ t find traces of compounds typical for the birch tar ( except a weak IR absorption in Sr765 ) . 
All the samples Sr765 - Sr770 are contaminated with minerals enriched in calcium . 
Calcium based minerals ( e.g . 
CaCO3 ) could be used more or less intentionally to neutralise organic acids formed during thermal decomposition of wood .
